17:523:35441:26:0:314:325:64:11:Times:11:Times:F:15
18:524:35443:0:17:136:561:708:13:Times:13:Times:A:cepts in five countries, Argentina, Chile, Colombia, Philippines and Pakistan, are
18:525:35525:17:19:136:562:691:13:Times:13:Times:A:significant at the 5% level and the correlation of the stock returns in these coun-
18:526:35608:19:20:136:562:672:13:Times:13:Times:A:tries is low. The multivariate intercept restrictions of Gibbons, Ross and Shanken
18:527:35690:20:19:136:562:652:14:Times:14:Times:C:(1989) adjusted for conditional heteroskedasticity and tested on the 8 countries
18:528:35770:19:17:136:562:633:13:Times:13:Times:A:with data from 1976:02 provides convincing evidence against the null hypothesis
18:529:35849:17:24:136:328:616:14:Times:14:Times:C:that the intercepts are equal to zero.
18:530:35887:24:19:159:563:592:13:Times:13:Times:A:The interesting finding is not just that the intercepts are significantly different
18:531:35970:19:19:135:563:573:14:Times:14:Times:C:from zero; the significant intercepts are all positive. Even if we use a different
18:532:36052:19:20:135:560:554:14:Times:14:Times:C:level of significance, say the one associated with t-ratios greater than 1.3 (10%
18:533:36133:20:19:135:561:534:14:Times:14:Times:C:level, one-sided), all 13 countries have positive intercepts. If the single factor
18:534:36215:19:19:135:559:515:13:Times:13:Times:A:CAPM describes world expected returns, this would imply that these countries'
18:535:36292:19:20:134:561:496:14:Times:14:Times:C:returns greatly exceeded expected levels of performance. Indeed, some of the
18:536:36368:20:17:134:559:476:14:Times:14:Times:C:pricing errors are massive. For example, Argentina's pricing error is 63.4% per
18:537:36447:17:20:134:559:459:14:Times:14:Times:C:annum with a t-ratio of 2.4 and Chile has an annualized error of 29.7% with a
18:538:36524:20:20:134:561:439:14:Times:14:Times:C:t-ratio of 2.9. Another possible interpretation is that the intercepts are telling us
18:539:36609:20:18:133:560:419:13:Times:13:Times:A:something about the survivorship bias problem. While the IFC started collecting
18:540:36688:18:19:133:560:401:14:Times:14:Times:C:data in 1981, the multivariate intercept tests reach back to 1976. However, an
18:541:36766:19:19:133:559:382:14:Times:14:Times:C:examination of the subperiod which does not include to Iookback bias period,
18:542:36842:19:21:133:489:363:13:Times:13:Times:A:suggests that survivorship does not completely explain the findings.
18:543:36910:21:20:157:560:342:13:Times:13:Times:A:Panel B of table 4 considers the most recent subperiod, 1986:03—1992:06.
18:544:36982:20:19:133:560:322:14:Times:14:Times:C:Five of the seven countries which had significant betas on the world index in
18:545:37059:19:20:133:557:303:13:Times:13:Times:A:the full sample have significant betas in the most recent sub-period.'3 Intercepts
18:546:37141:20:19:132:558:283:14:Times:14:Times:C:are significant at the 5% level in 7 of the 20 countries. 11 of the countries have
18:547:37223:19:19:132:558:264:14:Times:14:Times:C:intercepts with t-ratios greater than 1.3 and all of these intercepts are positive.
18:548:37306:19:19:132:558:245:14:Times:14:Times:C:Similar to the overall period, there are some countries withvery large pricing
18:549:37384:19:19:132:557:226:13:Times:13:Times:A:errors. For example, Chile has an error of 43.9% per annum with a t-ratio of 3.9.
18:550:37465:19:19:131:559:207:14:Times:14:Times:C:The multivariate test of Gibbons, Ross and Shanken (1989) provides evidence
18:551:37540:19:16:131:558:188:14:Times:14:Times:C:against the null hypothesis that the intercepts are zero for 18 countries at the
18:552:37620:16:25:131:186:172:12:Times:12:Times:F:0.1% level.
18:553:37631:25:19:155:556:147:13:Times:13:Times:A:The multivariate tests suggest that the world market portfolio is notuncon-
18:554:37706:19:19:139:556:128:13:Times:14:Times:A:13 Forsome of the countries, the full sample and the most recent subperiod
18:555:37780:19:30:130:238:109:13:Times:13:Times:A:sample are identical.
18:556:37801:30:0:337:348:79:11:Times:11:Times:F:16
19:557:37803:0:20:106:531:696:14:Times:14:Times:C:ditionally mean-variance efficient. This is in contrast to the findings of Cumby
19:558:37883:20:18:106:531:676:13:Times:13:Times:A:and Glen (1990) and Harvey (1991) who consider only developed market returns.
19:559:37960:18:20:106:533:658:14:Times:14:Times:C:The intercept tests suggest that the shift in the frontier documented in table 3
19:560:38040:20:19:106:534:638:13:Times:13:Times:A:was large enough that mean-variance efficiency can be rejected. Another way of
19:561:38118:19:20:106:531:619:14:Times:14:Times:C:interpreting this is finding is by examining the Kandel and Stambaugh (1989)
19:562:38194:20:21:106:231:599:13:Times:13:Times:A:critical rejection region.
19:563:38220:21:19:130:531:578:14:Times:14:Times:C:The solid hyperbola in first panel of figure 2 is the unconditional mean-
19:564:38293:19:19:105:532:559:13:Times:13:Times:B:variance frontierfor 36 assets from 1986:03—1992:06. The dashed hyperbola is
19:565:38369:19:19:106:533:540:14:Times:14:Times:C:the critical rejection region for a 5% significance level. Notice that the world
19:566:38449:19:19:106:534:521:13:Times:13:Times:A:market portfolio is well to the right of the critical rejection region indicating that
19:567:38535:19:19:106:532:502:13:Times:13:Times:A:this benchmark portfolio is significantly off the efficient frontier. The exercise is
19:568:38620:19:19:106:532:483:14:Times:14:Times:C:repeated in the second panel of figure 2 imposing the no short-sales restriction.
19:569:38701:19:19:106:533:464:13:Times:13:Times:A:While this does not correspond to the multivariate tests in table 4, it demonstrates
19:570:38785:19:20:106:534:445:14:Times:14:Times:C:that even if short-sale restrictions are imposed the world market portfolio is no
19:571:38866:20:22:106:352:425:13:Times:13:Times:A:where near the efficient portion of the frontier.
19:572:38915:22:18:130:531:403:13:Times:13:Times:A:The two-factor estimates over the full sample are presented in the right-hand
19:573:38992:18:21:106:532:385:14:Times:14:Times:C:columns of table 4. The world market beta remains significant at the 5% level
19:574:39069:21:18:106:534:364:14:Times:14:Times:C:in six countries: Mexico, Korea, Philippines, Malaysia, Thailand and Portugal.
19:575:39147:18:19:106:534:346:13:Times:13:Times:A:The foreign exchange risk factor has some explanatory power eight countries. It is
19:576:39229:19:19:106:532:327:13:Times:13:Times:A:especially important in explaining the aggregated index returns, Latin America,
19:577:39308:19:23:107:330:308:13:Times:13:Times:A:Asia and the emerging markets composite.
19:578:39348:23:19:131:531:285:14:Times:14:Times:C:The addition of this second factor, however, does not affect the intercepts.
19:579:39424:19:19:107:535:266:13:Times:13:Times:A:Five of the intercepts are significant (and positive) at the 5% level. Eleven have t-
19:580:39509:19:20:107:535:247:13:Times:13:Times:A:ratios greater than 1.3 and all of these are positive. The multivariate test provides
19:581:39594:20:22:107:471:227:13:Times:13:Times:A:evidence against the null hypotheses at the 1.4% level of significance.
19:582:39665:22:19:131:533:205:14:Times:14:Times:C:The currency risk factor appears to have more of an influence in the most
19:583:39738:19:19:107:534:186:13:Times:13:Times:A:recent sub-period. The right-hand columns of panel B show that this variable loads
19:584:39820:19:19:107:533:167:14:Times:14:Times:C:significantly into 7 countries' factor models: Chile, Mexico, Taiwan, Malaysia,
19:585:39899:19:19:107:532:148:13:Times:13:Times:A:Pakistan, Thailand and Zimbabwe. Both factors are important for the aggregated
19:586:39977:19:19:108:535:129:13:Times:13:Times:A:indices with 29% of the variance of the composite index explained. However, seven
19:587:40058:19:45:107:534:110:13:Times:13:Times:A:intercepts are significantly different from zero at the 5% level and 12 have t-ratios
19:588:40143:45:0:315:326:65:11:Times:11:Times:F:17
20:589:40145:0:20:133:559:704:14:Times:14:Times:C:greater than 1.3. All of these intercepts are positive. The multivariate intercept
20:590:40227:20:20:133:561:684:14:Times:14:Times:C:test provides evidence against the null hypothesis of zero intercepts at the .1%
20:591:40307:20:21:133:237:664:12:Times:12:Times:F:level of significance.
20:592:40329:21:19:157:561:643:13:Times:13:Times:A:Figure 3 presents these results using the Kandel and Stambaugh (1989) crit-
20:593:40404:19:19:133:560:624:14:Times:14:Times:C:ical rejection region for the two factor model. In the first panel, it is clear that
20:594:40488:19:19:133:559:605:14:Times:14:Times:C:portfolios of the world market return and the exchange rate return do not cross
20:595:40567:19:20:133:560:586:14:Times:14:Times:C:the critical rejection region drawn at the 5% significance level. With the short-
20:596:40648:20:18:133:561:566:13:Times:13:Times:A:sale restrictions imposed, the critical rejection region is intersected. However, as
20:597:40732:18:21:133:560:548:14:Times:14:Times:C:noted earlier, the asset pricing tests presented in table 4 allow for unrestricted
20:598:40814:21:21:133:200:527:13:Times:13:Times:A:short selling.
20:599:40828:21:20:157:561:506:13:Times:13:Times:A:Two additional world risk factors were considered.'4 In contrast to developing
20:600:40906:20:19:133:559:486:14:Times:14:Times:C:countries, many of the emerging markets have undiversified industrial sectors.
20:601:40984:19:19:134:562:467:13:Times:13:Times:A:Given that many of these equities are resource based, the emerging market equities
20:602:41066:19:19:133:559:448:13:Times:13:Times:A:may have significant exposure to price fluctuations in an index of natural resources.
20:603:41151:19:18:134:560:429:13:Times:13:Times:A:Bivariate regressions are estimated using the percentage change in the Commodity
20:604:41231:18:20:133:561:411:14:Times:14:Times:C:Research Bureau's (CRB) industrial inputs index in excess of a risk-free rate.
20:605:41309:20:19:133:561:391:14:Times:14:Times:C:There was only one country, Indonesia, that had a significant exposure to this
20:606:41387:19:22:134:167:372:13:Times:13:Times:A:factor.
20:607:41394:22:19:158:560:350:14:Times:14:Times:C:The emerging economies also have larger proportional agricultural sectors
20:608:41467:19:19:133:562:331:13:Times:13:Times:A:than the developed economies. Factor models were estimated using the percentage
20:609:41546:19:20:133:561:312:13:Times:13:Times:A:change CRB food price index in excess of a risk-free rate. Similar to the industrial
20:610:41630:20:22:133:511:292:13:Times:13:Times:A:input series, no country exhibited a significant sensitivity to this factor.
20:611:41706:22:19:158:560:270:13:Times:13:Times:A:Although the tests indicate that world market portfolio is inefficient, what is
20:612:41785:19:19:133:561:251:13:Times:13:Times:A:the cross-sectional relation between the expected returns and the risk sensitivities?
20:613:41870:19:19:133:560:232:14:Times:14:Times:C:Roll and Ross (1993) and Kandel and Stambaugh (1993) have recently shown
20:614:41942:19:19:134:560:213:14:Times:14:Times:C:that a small degree of inefficiency could result in no relation between expected
20:615:42022:19:31:133:560:194:13:Times:13:Times:A:returns and risks. The first panel of figure 4 provides a scatter plot of the average
20:616:42107:31:19:142:560:163:9:Times:13:Times:A:14Thesefactors were examined afterthefactor models were estimated in table
20:617:42181:19:14:133:561:144:14:Times:14:Times:C:4, in response to a suggestion by a conference discussant, and, as such, should
20:618:42260:14:16:133:560:130:13:Times:13:Times:A:not be considered factor snooping. Other specifications of global risk factors are
20:619:42342:16:12:133:560:114:13:Times:13:Times:A:investigated by Ferson and Harvey (1994a,b). The general approach follows Chen,
20:620:42421:12:29:133:247:102:13:Times:13:Times:A:Roll and Ross (1986).
20:621:42442:29:0:341:352:73:11:Times:11:Times:F:18
21:622:42444:0:19:104:530:699:13:Times:13:Times:B:returns and the world market betas over the recent subperiod. The cross-sectional
21:623:42525:19:19:104:531:680:14:Times:14:Times:C:regression line is also plotted and is insignificant. None of the cross-sectional
21:624:42606:19:19:104:530:661:13:Times:13:Times:B:variation is explained. If the loadings from the second risk factor are added to the
21:625:42690:19:24:104:427:642:13:Times:13:Times:B:estimation, the regression is still insignificant at the 5% level.
21:626:42756:24:18:129:529:618:13:Times:13:Times:A:The second panel of figure 4 presents the same average returns against their
21:627:42832:18:19:105:530:600:14:Times:14:Times:C:standard deviations. The cross-sectional regression line of the average returns
21:628:42911:19:18:105:533:581:14:Times:14:Times:C:on the volatilities is also presented with and without the influential Argentinian
21:629:42993:18:20:105:532:563:13:Times:13:Times:B:observation. The regression using all countries is significant at the 0.5% level. The
21:630:43078:20:20:105:531:543:13:Times:13:Times:B:own variance has more explanatory power than the beta with respect to the world
21:631:43157:20:19:105:531:523:14:Times:14:Times:C:portfolio. These results support the interpretation that many of the emerging
21:632:43234:19:21:106:428:504:13:Times:13:Times:A:markets are not fully integrated into world capital markets.'5
21:633:43296:21:19:130:532:483:13:Times:13:Times:A:There are other reasons why the unconditional CAPM could fail aside from
21:634:43368:19:19:106:532:464:13:Times:13:Times:A:the market integration issue. For example, the linear factor specification in table
21:635:43451:19:19:106:531:445:14:Times:14:Times:C:4 assumes that the conditional risk exposures are constant over the estimation
21:636:43529:19:20:106:534:426:14:Times:14:Times:C:period. The differences in the magnitude of the some of the risk coefficients in
21:637:43609:20:19:107:531:406:13:Times:13:Times:A:the full and most recent subperiod suggest that exposures may be time varying.
21:638:43687:19:19:107:533:387:13:Times:13:Times:A:Indeed, a rejection of the unconditional CAPM does not imply a rejection of the
21:639:43766:19:52:107:208:368:13:Times:13:Times:A:conditional CAPM.
21:640:43783:52:29:107:288:316:15:Times:15:Times:C:4. Analysis of conditional risk
21:641:43814:29:31:108:337:287:13:Times:13:Times:A:4.1 Predictable returns in emerging markets
21:642:43857:31:19:108:534:256:13:Times:13:Times:A:Table 5 presents an analysis of the predictable variation in the emerging market
21:643:43937:19:19:108:532:237:13:Times:13:Times:A:returns. Linear regressions of the emerging market returns on three setsof infor-
21:644:44018:19:19:108:532:218:13:Times:13:Times:A:mation variables are detailed. The first set consists of common worldinformation
21:645:44098:19:19:108:534:199:13:Times:13:Times:A:variables. The second includes only variables that are specific to the country being
21:646:44182:19:23:108:534:180:13:Times:13:Times:A:examined. The final set combines the local and country-specific information sets.
21:647:44263:23:33:132:533:157:13:Times:13:Times:A:To provide a direct comparison to research on developed markets, theworld
21:648:44336:33:14:133:533:124:13:Times:13:Times:A:Bekaert and Harvey (1993) present a model where the time-seriesof expected
21:649:44410:14:14:109:533:110:13:Times:13:Times:A:returns is generated by both the covariance with the world returnand the variance
21:650:44491:14:27:109:530:96:14:Times:14:Times:C:of the country return weighted by the probability that the market is integrated.
21:651:44571:27:0:316:327:69:11:Times:11:Times:F:19
22:652:44573:0:19:132:557:709:13:Times:14:Times:A:information set follows Harvey (1991).16Theset includes lagged values of the
22:653:44649:19:19:132:560:690:14:Times:14:Times:C:MSCI world return, the return on the U.S. three-month Treasury bill minus the
22:654:44726:19:19:132:558:671:14:Times:14:Times:C:one-month return, the yield spread between Moody's Baa and Aaa rated bonds
22:655:44800:19:19:132:558:652:13:Times:13:Times:A:and the Standard and Poor's 500 dividend yield minus the one-month U.S. Trea-
22:656:44877:19:19:131:558:633:13:Times:13:Times:A:sury bill return. The only difference between this information set and Harvey's is
22:657:44959:19:22:131:372:614:13:Times:13:Times:A:the exclusion of the January dummy variable.
22:658:45003:22:20:155:558:592:13:Times:13:Times:A:The first column of adjusted R2s results from regressions on the world infor-
22:659:45080:20:19:131:558:572:14:Times:14:Times:C:mation variables. Notice that the sample periods are slightly different than the
22:660:45160:19:18:131:557:553:13:Times:13:Times:A:table 4 regressiOns. This due to the unavailability of some of the local information
22:661:45244:18:21:131:556:535:13:Times:13:Times:A:variables which will be used in later analysis. Heteroskedasticity-consistent tests
22:662:45327:21:18:131:555:514:14:Times:14:Times:C:of significance (p-values) are reported beneath the R2. The expected returns in
22:663:45406:18:19:131:555:496:13:Times:13:Times:A:9 of the 20 countries are significantly (5% level) affected by the world informa-
22:664:45487:19:20:131:558:477:13:Times:13:Times:A:tion variables. A multivariate heteroskedasticity-consistent test of predictability
22:665:45570:20:18:130:556:457:13:Times:13:Times:A:based on the Pillai trace [see Kirby (1993)] provides strong evidence against the
22:666:45651:18:22:130:342:439:13:Times:13:Times:A:hypothesis of constant expected returns.
22:667:45691:22:19:154:557:417:13:Times:13:Times:A:The second column of adjusted R2s is obtained from regressions on the local
22:668:45766:19:20:130:555:398:13:Times:13:Times:A:information variables. The local information set includes the lagged country U.S.
22:669:45847:20:18:130:558:378:13:Times:13:Times:A:dollar returns, the change in the foreign exchange rate versus the U.S. dollar, the
22:670:45930:18:22:130:405:360:13:Times:13:Times:A:dividend yield and a local short-term interest rate. 17
22:671:45985:22:20:154:557:338:12:Helvetica:14:Times:C:Localinformation is important for 11 of the 20 regressions at the 5% level
22:672:46059:20:20:129:556:318:13:Times:13:Times:A:of significance. When the local information is combined with the world informa-
22:673:46138:20:19:130:556:298:14:Times:14:Times:C:tion, 12 regressions are significant at the 5% level and 14 at the 10% level. A
22:674:46217:19:19:130:556:279:13:Times:13:Times:A:heteroskedasticity-consistent exclusion test of the local information variables pro-
22:675:46301:19:33:129:555:260:14:Times:14:Times:C:vides evidence against the null hypothesis in 10 countries at the 5% level. That
22:676:46381:33:7:138:146:227:8:Times:8:Times:F:16
22:677:46383:7:15:153:556:220:12:Helvetica:13:Times:A:Harvey's(1991) selection of variables was motivated by Keim and Stambaugh
22:678:46456:15:7:129:415:205:13:Times:13:Times:A:(1986), Campbell (1987) and Fama and French (1988).
22:679:46507:7:21:137:555:198:9:Times:13:Times:A:17selected interest rates which were the 'most unregulated.' Deposit rates were
22:680:46586:21:13:129:555:177:13:Times:13:Times:A:used for Argentina, Chile, Colombia, Venezuela, Thailand, Greece, Jordan, and
22:681:46663:13:15:128:555:164:14:Times:14:Times:C:Nigeria. Call money rates were used in India, Indonesia, and Pakistan. Money
22:682:46739:15:14:129:556:149:13:Times:13:Times:A:market rates were used for Korea, Malaysia, and Turkey. Treasury bills were used
22:683:46819:14:14:128:554:135:14:Times:14:Times:C:for Mexico, Philippines, Portugal and Zimbabwe. The bank rate was used for
22:684:46893:14:12:128:554:121:13:Times:13:Times:A:Brazil. The U.S. three-month Treasury bill yield was used for Taiwan who is not
22:685:46972:12:30:128:375:109:13:Times:13:Times:A:a member of the International Monetary Fund.
22:686:47016:30:0:334:346:79:12:Times:12:Times:F:20
23:687:47018:0:19:103:531:695:13:Times:13:Times:B:is, in the 12 countries with significant regressions, 10 are importantly influenced
23:688:47101:19:19:103:528:676:14:Times:14:Times:C:by local information. The variance ratios in the far right-hand columns suggest
23:689:47180:19:20:103:530:657:13:Times:13:Times:B:that more than half of the predictable variance in these emerging market returns
23:690:47260:20:22:103:270:637:13:Times:13:Times:B:is induced by local information.
23:691:47292:22:19:128:532:615:14:Times:14:Times:C:From the evidence of serial correlation presented in table 1, it may seen-i
23:692:47367:19:20:103:530:596:14:Times:14:Times:C:obvious that lagged country returns should predict future returns. Indeed, it is
23:693:47447:20:19:103:529:576:13:Times:13:Times:B:possible that this type of predictability could be induced by infrequent trading.'8
23:694:47530:19:18:104:530:557:13:Times:13:Times:B:However, using a monthly frequency should diminish this influence. Interestingly,
23:695:47611:18:18:104:532:539:14:Times:14:Times:C:in the regressions with world and local information [not reported], only three
23:696:47689:18:20:104:530:521:13:Times:13:Times:B:countries, Colombia, Venezuela and the Philippines, have significant coefficients
23:697:47770:20:21:104:263:501:13:Times:13:Times:B:on the lagged country returns.
23:698:47800:21:22:128:531:480:14:Times:14:Times:C:These results contrast with the results on developed countries in three re-
23:699:47875:22:17:104:530:458:14:Times:14:Times:C:spects. First, the degree of explanatory power is greater in emerging markets.
23:700:47953:17:19:104:532:441:13:Times:13:Times:B:Using the combined information set, 7 of the regression adjusted R2 exceed 10%
23:701:48031:19:19:105:529:422:14:Times:14:Times:C:and 3 exceed 20%. Over the same period, the predictability of the world mar-
23:702:48107:19:19:105:530:403:13:Times:13:Times:B:ket portfolio is limited to 5%. Over the 1970.02—1989.5 period, Harvey (1991)
23:703:48184:19:18:105:531:384:13:Times:13:Times:B:reports that only 2 of 18 developed countries have adjusted R2s that exceed 10%
23:704:48263:18:19:105:532:366:13:Times:13:Times:B:using world information variables. Using various combinations of world and local
23:705:48343:19:23:105:419:347:13:Times:13:Times:B:information only three countries have R2s that exceed 10%.
23:706:48401:23:20:129:529:324:13:Times:13:Times:A:The second difference concerns the importance of local information variables.
23:707:48478:20:18:105:533:304:13:Times:13:Times:B:In almost all of the significant regressions, local information played an important
23:708:48561:18:20:106:533:286:14:Times:14:Times:C:role. In contrast, Harvey (1991) found that most of the variation was being
23:709:48636:20:19:106:533:266:14:Times:14:Times:C:driven by global information variables. Using a different sample and different
23:710:48714:19:20:106:532:247:13:Times:13:Times:A:instruments, Ferson and Harvey (1993) report that local information is important
23:711:48794:20:21:106:287:227:13:Times:13:Times:A:in only 6 of 18 developed markets.
23:712:48828:21:19:130:531:206:13:Times:13:Times:A:Some are skeptical of the predictability in asset returns because of the collec-
23:713:48908:19:37:106:533:187:13:Times:13:Times:A:tive data snooping by many researchers.19 While most of the snooping is focussed
23:714:48988:37:14:115:531:150:13:Times:13:Times:A:18 Serial correlation could be induced by persistence in country risk exposures
23:715:49067:14:14:106:531:136:13:Times:12:Times:A:or world risk premiums. It could also be induced by informationalinefficiencies.
23:716:49147:14:14:107:531:122:14:Times:14:Times:C:Unfortunately, there is no way to separate these possible causes and hence no
23:717:49224:14:15:107:325:108:14:Times:14:Times:C:attempt has been made to filter the data.
23:718:49265:15:28:115:355:93:13:Times:13:Times:A:19 See, for example, Foster and Smith (1993).
23:719:49310:28:0:314:325:65:11:Times:11:Times:F:21
24:720:49312:0:19:138:566:708:13:Times:13:Times:A:on U.S. returns, the use of international returns does not provide 'out-of-sample'
24:721:49394:19:18:138:564:689:14:Times:14:Times:C:evidence of predictability because of the correlation between the international
24:722:49473:18:20:138:564:671:14:Times:14:Times:C:returns and the U.S. return. For example, in Harvey (1991) the rank-order cor-
24:723:49551:20:18:138:565:651:14:Times:14:Times:C:relation between the predictive R2 and the squared correlation of the country
24:724:49628:18:21:138:563:633:14:Times:14:Times:C:returns with U.S. returns is 57.9% which is significant at the 5% level (p-value
24:725:49708:21:18:138:564:612:14:Times:14:Times:C:1.8%). That is, high correlation with the U.S. usually implies a high degree of
24:726:49787:18:22:137:209:594:13:Times:13:Times:A:predictability.
24:727:49802:22:20:161:563:572:14:Times:14:Times:C:The final contrast with developed markets is that there there is little or no
24:728:49879:20:18:137:564:552:14:Times:14:Times:C:relation between the predictability or emerging market returns and their uncon-
24:729:49958:18:19:137:563:534:14:Times:14:Times:C:ditional correlations with the U.S. or the world market return. The rank-order
24:730:50036:19:19:137:562:515:13:Times:13:Times:A:correlation between the predictive R2 and the squared correlation with the U.S.
24:731:50115:19:19:136:563:496:13:Times:13:Times:A:return is only 29.5% (p-value 22.0%). A similar result is obtained when one con-
24:732:50195:19:20:136:561:477:14:Times:14:Times:C:siders the squared correlation with the world market return. In thiscase, the
24:733:50272:20:19:136:562:457:14:Times:14:Times:C:rank-order correlation drops to -3.7% (p-value 88.0%). While this evidence is
24:734:50349:19:51:136:452:438:13:Times:13:Times:A:informal, it suggests that the predictability may be genuine.
24:735:50410:51:33:136:315:387:13:Times:13:Times:A:4.2 Conditional asset pricing tests
24:736:50445:33:18:135:563:354:13:Times:13:Times:A:Following the unconditional analysis in table 3, I examine the influences of two
24:737:50525:18:20:135:561:336:13:Times:13:Times:A:sources of risk, the world market return and the foreign exchange portfolio return,
24:738:50608:20:19:134:561:316:13:Times:13:Times:A:on conditionally expected returns. In this analysis, expected returns, risk premi-
24:739:50690:19:23:135:549:297:13:Times:13:Times:A:ums and betas change through time as a function of the information variables.
24:740:50767:23:19:158:560:274:16:Times:13:Times:A:Let Z', Zt,be the world information, local information and the com-
24:741:50834:19:14:134:478:255:13:Times:13:Times:A:bined information respectively. The following model is estimated:

24:747:50991:19:18:133:558:127:13:Times:13:Times:A:where r represents the return on asset i, ö are coefficients froma linear projection
24:748:51075:18:29:132:558:109:13:Times:14:Times:A:of the asset returns on the information,are the fitted conditional betas, f
24:749:51150:29:0:339:350:80:11:Times:11:Times:F:22
25:750:51152:0:20:108:534:700:13:Times:13:Times:A:are the factor returns, U are the coefficients from a linear projection of the factor
25:751:51237:20:18:108:534:680:14:Times:14:Times:C:returns on the information, p is the mean asset return, and a is the difference
25:752:51316:18:21:108:533:662:14:Times:14:Times:C:between the mean asset return and the model fitted mean asset return (pricing
25:753:51393:21:18:108:532:641:14:Times:13:Times:A:error). Conditioning t and u3 on Zw,t,U2Ofl ZDandu4 and u5 on ones produces
25:754:51468:18:22:108:336:623:13:Times:13:Times:A:an exactly identified system of equations.2°
25:755:51512:22:19:132:534:601:14:Times:14:Times:C:The following is the intuition behind the system. The first two equations
25:756:51585:19:19:108:532:582:14:Times:14:Times:C:are regressions of the asset and factor returns on the information. These are
25:757:51662:19:20:108:532:563:14:Times:14:Times:C:'statistical' models of expected returns. I let the country returns be influenced
25:758:51743:20:19:107:532:543:14:Times:14:Times:C:by both local and world information variables. However, the world risk premi-
25:759:51820:19:19:107:534:524:13:Times:13:Times:A:ums are strictly a function of world information variables. Next the definition of
25:760:51902:19:26:107:236:505:13:Times:13:Times:A:conditional beta is used:
25:761:51927:26:9:270:332:479:11:Times:13:Helvetica:C:/wt —1Fwe= (E[u2u2tIZ....,})
25:762:51955:9:28:346:530:470:17:Times:12:Times:C:E[ftuiIZ_i].(5)
25:763:51970:28:19:107:532:442:14:Times:14:Times:C:The conditional beta in (4) is assumed to be a linear function of the combined
25:764:52048:19:19:107:534:423:13:Times:13:Times:A:world and local information.2' The last two equations deliver the average pricing
25:765:52129:19:19:107:532:404:14:Times:14:Times:C:error. Parameter p is the average expected return from the statistical model.
25:766:52206:19:19:107:533:385:13:Times:13:Times:A:The parameter a is the difference between the average 'statistical' model returns
25:767:52287:19:19:107:532:366:14:Times:14:Times:C:and the asset pricing model's fitted returns. It is analogous to the a reported in
25:768:52369:19:19:107:532:347:13:Times:13:Times:A:table 3. However, in this analysis, both the betas and the premiums are changing
25:769:52449:19:23:107:530:328:13:Times:13:Times:A:through time. Furthermore, the focus is on the predictable portion of the returns.
25:770:52531:23:19:131:531:305:14:Times:14:Times:C:This complicated system of equations and can only be estimated one asset
25:771:52603:19:19:107:532:286:13:Times:13:Times:A:at a time. As such, not all the cross-sectional restrictions of asset pricing theory
25:772:52687:19:19:107:532:267:13:Times:13:Times:A:can be imposed. For example, it will not be possible to report a multivariate test
25:773:52769:19:19:107:531:248:14:Times:14:Times:C:of whether the cx parameters are equal to zero. However, one important cross-
25:774:52846:19:20:106:531:229:13:Times:13:Times:A:sectional restriction has been imposed. Because the system is exactly identified,
25:775:52927:20:20:107:531:209:14:Times:13:Times:A:the world risk premium function, Z,9,isidentical for every country examined.
25:776:53003:20:18:115:531:189:9:Times:13:Times:A:20Foranalysis of related systems, see Ferson (1990), Harvey (1992), Ferson and
25:777:53081:18:14:107:532:171:13:Times:13:Times:A:Korajzcyk (1993) and Ferson and Harvey (1993). Importantly, I ask the model to
25:778:53159:14:16:107:531:157:13:Times:13:Times:A:explain the predictability induced by both local and world information whereas
25:779:53237:16:13:107:531:141:13:Times:13:Times:A:Ferson and Harvey (1993) only challenge the model to explain the predictability
25:780:53316:13:14:107:285:128:13:Times:13:Times:A:induced by the world information.
25:781:53349:14:18:115:531:114:14:Times:14:Times:C:21 The linear conditional beta formulation is used in Shanken (1990), Ferson
25:782:53425:18:27:107:427:96:13:Times:13:Times:A:and Harvey (1991, 1993) and Jagannathan and Wang (1993).
25:783:53481:27:0:313:325:69:12:Times:12:Times:F:23
26:784:53483:0:19:157:559:707:14:Times:14:Times:C:The conditional risk function is simply Z,c,.Waldtests are conducted to
26:785:53554:19:19:133:560:688:13:Times:13:Times:A:test for the significance of the beta and to test whether the beta changes through
26:786:53636:19:22:133:159:669:13:Times:13:Times:A:time.
26:787:53641:22:19:157:559:647:14:Times:14:Times:C:As this system is exactly identified, there is no general test of the model's
26:788:53718:19:19:133:561:628:13:Times:13:Times:A:restrictions in the form of Hansen's (1982) J-statistic. However, the asset pricing
26:789:53801:19:19:133:559:609:14:Times:14:Times:C:model implies that the coefficient cshouldnot be different from zero and this
26:790:53878:19:19:133:559:590:14:Times:14:Times:C:hypothesis can be tested. Another possible test involves analyzing the model
26:791:53954:19:24:132:196:571:13:Times:13:Times:A:disturbance:

26:805:54814:23:20:155:557:281:13:Times:13:Times:A:The Wald tests show that, in four of the countries, the conditional betas are
26:806:54891:20:19:130:555:261:14:Times:14:Times:C:significantly different from zero. In three of these countries, the betas exhibit

26:808:55054:19:19:130:556:223:14:Times:14:Times:C:explain the predictability in the asset returns. For the countries that have sig-
26:809:55135:19:19:130:556:204:14:Times:14:Times:C:nificant time-variation in their expected returns, not only are the pricing errors
26:810:55217:19:18:130:555:185:13:Times:13:Times:A:different from zero on average, they are correlated with the predetermined infor-
26:811:55298:18:20:130:556:167:13:Times:13:Times:A:mation. These correlations are sufficient to a provide rejection of the asset pricing
26:812:55383:20:21:129:216:147:13:Times:13:Times:A:specification (4).

26:815:55555:28:0:336:348:78:12:Times:12:Times:F:24
27:816:55557:0:19:132:532:694:13:Times:13:Times:A:The results of the two-factor estimation are presented in panel B. In six of the
27:817:55637:19:19:108:535:675:13:Times:13:Times:A:eight countries, the average pricing errors are worse with two factors rather than

27:820:55888:19:20:108:535:619:14:Times:14:Times:C:factor reduces the residual R2 on the combined information in four of the five
27:821:55966:20:18:108:534:599:13:Times:13:Times:A:countries with time-varying betas. However, the correlation between the pricing
27:822:56045:18:23:108:533:581:13:Times:13:Times:A:errors and the combined information is still significant for three of the countries.
27:823:56129:23:19:132:533:558:14:Times:14:Times:C:Figure 4 provides plots of the conditional betas from the single factor esti-
27:824:56206:19:20:108:535:539:13:Times:13:Times:A:mation along with 60-month rolling correlations calculated with and without the
27:825:56285:20:19:108:533:519:13:Times:13:Times:A:October 1987 observation. For most of the countries, the general movements in
27:826:56362:19:20:108:536:500:14:Times:14:Times:C:the conditional betas are reflected in the rolling correlation measure (which is
27:827:56442:20:19:108:533:480:14:Times:14:Times:C:smoother due to the overlapping samples). This is especially true in the coun-
27:828:56520:19:19:108:536:461:13:Times:13:Times:A:tries with the most significantly time-varying betas, Argentina, Mexico, India and
27:829:56602:19:22:108:159:442:14:Times:14:Times:C:Thailand.
27:830:56611:22:19:132:534:420:14:Times:14:Times:C:The behavior of the correlations and the relation between the correlations
27:831:56685:19:19:108:533:401:13:Times:13:Times:A:and market betas is important because some observers interpret increased corre-
27:832:56764:19:18:109:533:382:13:Times:13:Times:A:lation as evidence of increased market integration. From figure 4, the numerical
27:833:56844:18:19:109:535:364:13:Times:13:Times:A:magnitude of the correlation has increased in five countries: Brazil, Chile, Mex-
27:834:56925:19:19:109:536:345:13:Times:13:Times:A:ico, Korea and Thailand. However, there is no necessary link between correlation
27:835:57005:19:19:109:534:326:13:Times:13:Times:A:and integration. A country can have zero correlation with the world market and
27:836:57083:19:19:109:535:307:13:Times:13:Times:A:be perfectly integrated into world capital markets. The low correlation could be
27:837:57163:19:20:109:535:288:13:Times:13:Times:A:caused by the weighted average of the firm betas in the country index equalling
27:838:57242:20:22:109:133:268:12:Times:12:Times:F:zero.
27:839:57247:22:19:133:535:246:13:Times:13:Times:A:Table 7 sheds some light on the relation between correlation and beta. Inter-
27:840:57324:19:19:109:535:227:13:Times:13:Times:A:estingly, the unconditional correlation is significantly different from zero in only
27:841:57408:19:19:110:534:208:13:Times:13:Times:A:three countries: Mexico, Korea, and Thailand. A test of whether this correlation
27:842:57488:19:19:110:535:189:13:Times:13:Times:A:is time-varying produces no evidence against the null hypothesis of constant cor-
27:843:57569:19:20:110:538:170:13:Times:13:Times:A:relation, however, the lowest p-values are found for Chile, Mexico, Korea, India
27:844:57649:20:29:110:193:150:13:Times:13:Times:A:and Thailand.23
27:845:57664:29:14:118:537:121:13:Times:13:Times:A:23 The test measures whether the unconditional correlation is constant. A differ-
27:846:57745:14:15:110:536:107:13:Times:13:Times:A:ent and more complex test is whether the conditional correlation is constant. This
27:847:57827:15:28:110:537:92:13:Times:13:Times:A:is more complex because it is necessary to model the dynamics of the conditional
27:848:57907:28:0:317:329:64:12:Times:12:Times:F:25
28:849:57909:0:19:156:558:707:13:Times:13:Times:A:The correlation is related to beta by the ratio the world and country standard
28:850:57987:19:22:132:560:688:13:Times:13:Times:A:deviations. Table 7 tests whether the ratio of variances is constant in the following
28:851:58072:22:13:131:170:666:13:Times:13:Times:A:system:

28:858:58270:19:24:131:442:543:13:Times:13:Times:A:of whether this ratio is constant with 8 degrees of freedom.
28:859:58330:24:18:155:557:519:14:Times:14:Times:C:This decomposition helps interpret the observation that correlations of the
28:860:58405:18:18:131:555:501:13:Times:13:Times:A:emerging market returns and the world market return are shifting through time.
28:861:58483:18:19:131:556:483:14:Times:14:Times:C:For three of the countries, Argentina, Chile and Thailand there is evidence in
28:862:58561:19:20:131:555:464:13:Times:13:Times:A:table 7 against the null hypothesis that the ratio of variances is constant. For two
28:863:58645:20:19:130:558:444:13:Times:13:Times:A:other countries, Mexico and India, the evidence in table 6 suggests that the con-
28:864:58726:19:17:130:556:425:13:Times:13:Times:A:ditional betas are changing through time. Each or both of these two effects could
28:865:58807:17:20:130:555:408:13:Times:14:Times:A:cause time-variation in correlations —orthey could cancel each other out. But,
28:866:58885:20:19:130:557:388:13:Times:13:Times:A:importantly, the correlation measure, the ratio of volatilities, and the conditional
28:867:58969:19:19:130:557:369:13:Times:13:Times:A:betas, are not sufficient to make inference about the degree of integration in these
28:868:59053:19:54:130:214:350:13:Times:13:Times:A:capital markets.
28:869:59069:54:32:130:437:296:13:Times:13:Times:A:4.3 Future directions for asset pricing in emerging markets
28:870:59128:32:19:129:557:264:14:Times:14:Times:C:In contrast to the evidence in developed markets, the global unconditional as-
28:871:59206:19:19:129:555:245:13:Times:13:Times:A:set pricing models are unable to explain the cross-section of expected returns in
28:872:59287:19:19:129:554:226:14:Times:14:Times:C:emerging markets. Also different from the evidence in developed markets, the
28:873:59363:19:19:129:557:207:14:Times:14:Times:C:analysis of conditional risk and risk premiums suggests that significant pricing
28:874:59443:19:19:129:555:188:14:Times:14:Times:C:errors persist and the standard asset pricing models do not account for the pre-
28:875:59523:19:19:129:555:169:14:Times:14:Times:C:dictability in the emerging market returns. One likely factor contributing to the
28:876:59604:19:18:129:553:150:13:Times:13:Times:A:failure of these models is the lack of integration of the emerging markets into the
28:877:59687:18:27:128:246:132:13:Times:13:Times:A:world capital markets.
28:878:59709:27:28:128:464:105:13:Times:13:Times:A:variance processes for both the country and the world portfolio.
28:879:59773:28:0:334:346:77:12:Times:12:Times:F:26
29:880:59775:0:20:135:537:694:14:Times:14:Times:C:Indeed, there are significant barriers to free capital flows in many of the
29:881:59850:20:18:110:537:674:13:Times:13:Times:A:countries in the sample. For example, foreigners could not directly participate in
29:882:59932:18:20:111:537:656:14:Times:14:Times:C:the Korean equity market. While the strict controls were dismantled at the end
29:883:60010:20:21:110:537:636:13:Times:13:Times:A:of 1992 [see Chuppe and Atkin (1992)], the Korean market is effectively off limits
29:884:60092:21:20:111:235:615:13:Times:13:Times:A:throughout our sample.
29:885:60114:20:19:135:537:595:14:Times:14:Times:C:There are other countries which have two classes of trading. For example,
29:886:60187:19:19:111:537:576:14:Times:14:Times:C:in Thailand, identical stocks trade on Main (for domestic investors) and Alien
29:887:60265:19:21:111:538:557:13:Times:13:Times:A:(for foreign investors) Boards. Foreigners are restricted to a certain proportion of
29:888:60349:21:18:111:537:536:14:Times:14:Times:C:the capitalization (which depends on the industry). Bailey and Jagtiani (1993)
29:889:60427:18:21:111:537:518:13:Times:13:Times:A:show that the Alien-Main premium is significantly different from zero and changes
29:890:60508:21:20:111:183:497:13:Times:13:Times:A:through time.
29:891:60521:20:20:135:536:477:14:Times:14:Times:C:The segmentation of these markets make it unlikely that expected returns
29:892:60593:20:20:111:536:457:14:Times:14:Times:C:will adhere to a global asset pricing model. In a completely segmented market,
29:893:60671:20:18:111:539:437:13:Times:13:Times:A:own volatility (which is usually idiosyncratic in a global asset pricing model) may
29:894:60754:18:19:111:539:419:13:Times:13:Times:A:be priced.24 Indeed, the evidence in figure 4 is suggestive of a relation between
29:895:60835:19:18:112:537:400:13:Times:13:Times:A:own volatility and the cross-section of expected returns. In a segmented market,
29:896:60915:18:20:112:538:382:13:Times:13:Times:A:covariance with global factors may appear to be priced to the extent that there is
29:897:60997:20:23:112:457:362:13:Times:13:Times:A:correlation between the local market volatility and global factors.
29:898:61064:23:18:136:539:339:13:Times:13:Times:A:Empirical asset pricing research has either assumed complete segmentation
29:899:61137:18:21:113:538:321:13:Times:13:Times:A:[for example, Black, Jensen and Scholes (1972), Fama and MacBeth (1973), Gib-
29:900:61214:21:17:112:539:300:13:Times:13:Times:A:bons (1982) and Stambaugh (1982)], complete integration [for example, Harvey
29:901:61290:17:20:113:537:283:14:Times:13:Helvetica:C:(1991), Dumas and Solnik (1993) and this paper], or a combination —partial
29:902:61364:20:19:113:540:263:14:Times:14:Times:C:segmentation. None of these models accounts for time-varying integration. A
29:903:61439:19:19:113:540:244:13:Times:13:Times:A:reasonable prior (especially with emerging markets) is to expect a high degree of
29:904:61520:19:20:113:540:225:14:Times:14:Times:C:segmentation early in the market history and increasing integration with world
29:905:61598:20:21:113:345:205:13:Times:13:Times:A:capital markets as we approach present day.
29:906:61641:21:18:137:537:184:13:Times:13:Times:A:An asset pricing specification that allows for time-varying integration should
29:907:61719:18:58:113:540:166:14:Times:14:Times:C:let both the covariance with the world market and the covariance with the local
29:908:61798:58:18:121:538:108:14:Times:14:Times:C:24 See, for example, Errunza and Losq (1985) and Eun and Janakiramanan
29:909:61868:18:27:114:334:90:13:Times:13:Times:A:(1986) for models of partial segmentation.
29:910:61910:27:0:321:332:63:11:Times:11:Times:F:27
30:911:61912:0:25:129:367:705:13:Times:13:Times:A:market return to affect the conditional mean:
30:912:61957:25:30:188:553:680:16:Times:12:Helvetica:C:=— &t).1Covt_i[rt,r]— (1—t))4_1Covt_i[rt,rt](8)
30:913:62004:30:19:129:555:650:14:Times:14:Times:C:where r3isthe return on security jincountry i, r1isthe return on the local
30:914:62078:19:17:129:554:631:13:Times:13:Times:A:country index, cbtisthe measure of time-varying integration (1= complete inte-
30:915:62156:17:19:128:554:614:13:Times:13:Times:A:gration, 0=complete segmentation), and ) is a measure of risk aversion (w=global,
30:916:62237:19:20:129:555:595:13:Times:13:Times:A:i=country specific). The key to estimating this type of model is the specification
30:917:62319:20:53:128:539:575:24:Times:13:Times:A:of .Thisresearch direction is being pursued in Bekaert and Harvey (1993).
30:918:62392:53:31:129:218:522:15:Times:15:Times:C:5. Conclusions
30:919:62406:31:19:152:554:491:13:Times:13:Times:A:This paper provides the first comprehensive analysis of 20 new equity mar-
30:920:62480:19:20:128:555:472:13:Times:13:Times:A:kets in emerging economies. These markets have historically been characterized
30:921:62558:20:18:128:556:452:13:Times:13:Times:A:by high average returns and large volatility. However, given the low correlation
30:922:62638:18:18:128:556:434:13:Times:13:Times:A:with developed country returns, the evidence suggests that the emerging market
30:923:62716:18:19:128:555:416:14:Times:14:Times:C:returns are not spanned by the developed market returns. As a result, inclusion
30:924:62795:19:19:128:553:397:13:Times:13:Times:A:of emerging market assets in a mean-variance efficient portfolio will significantly
30:925:62878:19:23:128:426:378:13:Times:13:Times:A:reduce portfolio volatility and increase expected returns.
30:926:62936:23:19:152:554:355:14:Times:14:Times:C:Next, the risk of emerging market equities is analyzed. Risk exposure is
30:927:63008:19:20:128:555:336:13:Times:13:Times:A:interlinked with asset pricing theory. That is, exposure is only meaningful if it is
30:928:63092:20:18:128:552:316:13:Times:13:Times:A:rewarded in equilibrium. However, equilibrium models of global asset pricing take,
30:929:63174:18:19:127:555:298:14:Times:14:Times:C:as given, the complete integration of world capital markets. Applying standard
30:930:63252:19:19:127:552:279:14:Times:14:Times:C:one and two-factor global asset pricing paradigms leads to large pricing errors.
30:931:63332:19:18:127:553:260:14:Times:14:Times:C:The betas are unable to explain any of the cross-sectional variation in expected
30:932:63412:18:25:127:168:242:14:Times:14:Times:C:returns.
30:933:63420:25:19:151:554:217:14:Times:14:Times:C:Finally, the predictability of the emerging market returns is investigated.
30:934:63495:19:18:127:554:198:13:Times:13:Times:A:Both world and local information variables are used to forecast the returns. There
30:935:63577:18:20:127:554:180:14:Times:14:Times:C:are three important differences between the predictability in emerging and in
30:936:63654:20:18:127:554:160:13:Times:13:Times:A:developed markets. First, in developed markets, the market's correlation with the
30:937:63735:18:19:127:553:142:13:Times:13:Times:A:U.S. return is closely linked to the degree of predictability. In emerging markets,
30:938:63818:19:19:127:552:123:13:Times:13:Times:A:there is no significant association between correlation with the U.S. portfolio and
30:939:63901:19:28:126:554:104:13:Times:13:Times:A:predictability. Second, the amount of predictability found in the emerging markets
30:940:63983:28:0:333:345:76:12:Times:12:Times:F:28
31:941:63985:0:20:115:541:692:13:Times:13:Times:A:is greater than that found in developed markets. Third, local information variables
31:942:64068:20:18:114:543:672:13:Times:13:Times:A:play a much more important role in predicting emerging market returns. Indeed,
31:943:64146:18:18:114:541:654:13:Times:13:Times:A:over half of the predictable variance in the emerging market returns can be traced
31:944:64228:18:25:114:221:636:13:Times:13:Times:A:to local information.
31:945:64249:25:17:138:543:611:14:Times:14:Times:C:Predictability can be induced by time-varying risk premiums, time-varying
31:946:64322:17:19:114:542:594:13:Times:13:Times:A:risk exposures or a combination of the two. Given the nature of the predictability,
31:947:64405:19:20:114:540:575:13:Times:13:Times:A:in that it is strongly influenced by local information, it is most likely driven time-
31:948:64491:20:18:114:540:555:14:Times:14:Times:C:varying risk exposures. When a model is estimated that allows for all of the
31:949:64567:18:20:114:542:537:14:Times:14:Times:C:moments to change through time, there is some evidence of time-varying risk
31:950:64642:20:18:114:542:517:13:Times:13:Times:A:exposures. However, the conditional asset pricing models fail to price the emerging
31:951:64725:18:19:114:539:499:13:Times:13:Times:A:market assets correctly on average and are unable to account for the time variation
31:952:64808:19:23:113:218:480:13:Times:13:Times:A:in expected returns.
31:953:64828:23:19:137:539:457:13:Times:13:Times:A:The fact that much of the predictability is induced by local information is also
31:954:64908:19:19:113:539:438:14:Times:14:Times:C:consistent with the possibility that some of these countries are segmented from
31:955:64987:19:20:113:540:419:13:Times:13:Times:A:world capital markets. Future research will investigate an asset pricing framework
31:956:65069:20:20:113:541:399:14:Times:14:Times:C:that allows for the possibility of incomplete integration and for the degree of
31:957:65148:20:317:113:300:379:13:Times:13:Times:A:integration to change through time.

35:1108:75191:11:16:146:494:426:11:Times:11:Times:F:Model: A Sensitivity Analysis, Journal of Financial Economics 10, 237—268.

36:1115:75577:0:27:125:469:709:14:Times:14:Times:C:Appendix: IFC Indices and Restrictions on Foreign Investors
36:1116:75636:27:13:136:553:682:13:Times:13:Times:A:The International Finance Corporation (IFC) began calculating market indices in
36:1117:75715:13:13:125:553:669:13:Times:13:Times:A:1981. The indices, known as the IFC Global (IFCG) Indices, do not take into consid-
36:1118:75798:13:13:124:553:656:13:Times:13:Times:A:eration restrictions on foreign ownership. While there is a trend towards reducing the
36:1119:75884:13:18:124:537:643:12:Times:12:Times:F:barriers to foreign ownership, these constraints are binding in a number of countries.
36:1120:75970:18:13:136:550:625:13:Times:13:Times:A:Recently, the IFC has introduced a second set of indices, the IFC Investable (IFCI)
36:1121:76053:13:13:124:553:612:12:Times:12:Times:F:Indices. The IFCI indices reflect restrictions on ownership limits. For example, if a firm
36:1122:76143:13:13:124:552:599:13:Times:13:Times:A:had a market capitalization of US $300 million and the national law restricts foreign
36:1123:76228:13:13:124:552:586:12:Times:12:Times:F:ownership to 50% of any company, the IFC Global index uses the full $300 million as
36:1124:76311:13:18:124:491:573:12:Times:12:Times:F:the market capitalization while the IFC Investable index uses $150 million.
36:1125:76386:18:13:136:550:555:13:Times:13:Times:A:Since my paper studies the integration of the emerging markets into world capital
36:1126:76467:13:13:124:550:542:12:Times:12:Times:F:markets, I have chosen to use the IFC Global indices. An additional reason for using the
36:1127:76555:13:14:124:551:529:12:Times:12:Times:F:Global indices is the limited availability of the Investable indices (data begins in 1988).
36:1128:76646:14:13:123:552:515:13:Times:13:Times:A:However, it is important to understand the degree of restrictions in each market. The
36:1129:76731:13:26:124:483:502:12:Times:12:Times:F:following is drawn from the International Finance Corporation (1993a).25
36:1130:76803:26:14:124:551:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:Argentina. The market is considered generally 100% investable; some corporate statue
36:1131:76887:14:17:124:208:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:limitations apply.
36:1132:76905:17:13:124:549:445:12:Times:12:Times:F:Brazil. The market is considered generally investable. Since May 1991 foreign institu-
36:1133:76991:13:13:124:551:432:12:Times:12:Times:F:tions may own up to 49% of voting common stock and 100% of non-voting participating
36:1134:77074:13:15:123:551:419:13:Times:13:Times:A:preferred stock. Some corporate statue limitations (e.g., Petrobras common are off-
36:1135:77157:15:15:124:187:404:12:Times:12:Times:F:limits) apply.
36:1136:77171:15:14:124:553:389:12:Times:12:Times:F:Chile. Foreign portfolio investment is considered to enter Chile through Law 18657 of
36:1137:77256:14:12:124:551:375:12:Times:12:Times:F:1987 regarding Foreign Capital Investment Funds, which limits aggregate foreign own-
36:1138:77340:12:18:124:333:363:12:Times:12:Times:F:ership to 25% of a listed company's shares.
36:1139:77383:18:18:124:496:345:12:Times:12:Times:F:Colombia. The market is considered 100% investable from February 1, 1991.
36:1140:77456:18:18:123:364:327:12:Times:12:Times:F:Greece. The market is generally 100% investable.
36:1141:77504:18:13:123:550:309:12:Times:12:Times:F:India. A press release issued by the Ministry of Finance of the Government of India on
36:1142:77590:13:13:123:549:296:12:Times:12:Times:F:September 14, 1992 announced that foreign institutional investors (Fils) could henceforth
36:1143:77679:13:13:123:552:283:12:Times:12:Times:F:invest in all listed securities in both primary and secondary markets. FITs are required to
36:1144:77770:13:13:123:550:270:12:Times:12:Times:F:register with the Securities and Exchange Board of India before making any investment.
36:1145:77856:13:13:123:552:257:13:Times:13:Times:A:The market is considered effectively open from November 1, 1992. Investments are
36:1146:77936:13:14:123:549:244:12:Times:12:Times:F:subject to a ceiling of 24% of issued share capital for the total holdings of all registered
36:1147:78028:14:13:123:550:230:12:Times:12:Times:F:FIls and 5% for the holding of a single FIT in any one company. The ceiling includes the
36:1148:78116:13:18:123:496:217:12:Times:12:Times:F:conversion of fully and partly convertible debentures issued by the company.
36:1149:78192:18:12:123:551:199:12:Times:12:Times:F:Indonesia. Until December 1987, the market was closed to foreign investment. In Decem-
36:1150:78278:12:14:123:551:187:12:Times:12:Times:F:ber 1987, the government introduced deregulation measures that allowed foreigners to
36:1151:78362:14:13:123:550:173:12:Times:12:Times:F:purchase shares in eight non-joint venture companies. On September 16, 1989, the Minis-
36:1152:78449:13:13:123:551:160:12:Times:12:Times:F:ter of Finance of the Republic of Indonesia issued Decree Number 1055/KMK.013/1989,
36:1153:78532:13:19:123:550:147:12:Times:12:Times:F:which allowed foreigners to purchase up to 49% of all companies' listed shares, including
36:1154:78621:19:21:119:551:128:9:Times:13:Times:A:25Alsosee Castelin and Stone (1990). Gooptu (1993) provides a comprehensive
36:1155:78696:21:29:123:434:107:13:Times:13:Times:A:analysis of portfolio investment flows to emerging markets.
36:1156:78755:29:0:330:341:78:11:Times:11:Times:F:34
37:1157:78757:0:13:118:546:694:12:Times:12:Times:F:forcigii joint ventures but excluding banks. The Bank Act, 1992, enacted on October 30,
37:1158:78844:13:14:118:544:681:12:Times:12:Times:F:1992, allowed foreigners to invest in up to 49% of the listed shares in three categories
37:1159:78932:14:12:117:544:667:12:Times:12:Times:F:of banks-private national, state and joint foreign. Currently only private national banks
37:1160:79021:12:13:118:546:655:12:Times:12:Times:F:are listed. %In a few markets, such as Indonesia, companies do not %list all the shares
37:1161:79108:13:16:117:545:642:12:Times:12:Times:F:outstanding. %For its indexes, IFC counts only the shares listed %at the stock exchange.
37:1162:79196:16:20:118:407:626:12:Times:12:Times:F:Jordan. The market is considered generally 49% investable.
37:1163:79254:20:12:117:545:606:12:Times:12:Times:F:Korea. Since January 1, 1992, authorized foreign investors have been allowed to acquire
37:1164:79341:12:14:117:544:594:13:Times:13:Times:A:up to 10% of the capital of listed companies; some corporate statue limitations apply
37:1165:79426:14:12:118:542:580:13:Times:13:Times:A:(e.g. POSCO and KEPCO 8%, and some are permitted up to 25%). The 10% limit
37:1166:79500:12:14:117:546:568:13:Times:13:Times:A:applies separately to common and preferred stock. Under the revised regulations of
37:1167:79582:14:12:117:545:554:12:Times:12:Times:F:June 22, 1992, effective in July 1992, companies whose foreign holdings already exceed
37:1168:79668:12:13:117:543:542:12:Times:12:Times:F:10% could apply to Korea's Securities and Exchange Commission to increase their limit
37:1169:79753:13:15:117:543:529:12:Times:12:Times:F:to 25%. As of March 1993, four companies had received permission: Korea Electronic
37:1170:79835:15:12:117:544:514:12:Times:12:Times:F:Parts, Korea Long-Term Credit Bank, Trigem Computer and Young Chang Akki. The
37:1171:79912:12:18:116:532:502:12:Times:12:Times:F:ceiling automatically declines when foreign-held shares are sold to domestic investors.
37:1172:79999:18:13:117:542:484:12:Times:12:Times:F:Malaysia. The limit on foreign ownership of Malaysian stocks is subject to some debate.
37:1173:80086:13:13:117:544:471:13:Times:13:Times:A:Bank Negara, the central bank, restricts the ownership of banks and financial institu-
37:1174:80172:13:13:116:541:458:12:Times:12:Times:F:tions by foreigners to 30%. However, these limits do not appear to be strictly enforced.
37:1175:80260:13:13:116:541:445:12:Times:12:Times:F:Under the Bankings and Financial Institutions Act, 1989, the approval of the Minister
37:1176:80345:13:13:116:544:432:12:Times:12:Times:F:of Finance is required before foreign investors can buy or sell shares of a licensed bank of
37:1177:80437:13:13:116:542:419:12:Times:12:Times:F:finance company amounting to 5% or more. Certain non-bank stocks have different for-
37:1178:80521:13:13:116:543:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:eign share holdings limits for tax and other reasons. These are MISC, Proton, Telekom,
37:1179:80607:13:13:116:543:393:13:Times:13:Times:A:Tenaga Nasional, Tai Wah Garments and Yantzekiang. All other stocks are open to
37:1180:80686:13:13:116:542:380:12:Times:12:Times:F:foreign portfolio investment without any limits. However, the approval of the Foreign
37:1181:80771:13:13:116:543:367:12:Times:12:Times:F:Investment Committee is required for acquiring 15% or more of the voting power of a
37:1182:80854:13:14:115:544:354:12:Times:12:Times:F:company by any one foreign interest and for acquiring the assets of interests of a com-
37:1183:80941:14:12:115:543:340:12:Times:12:Times:F:pany when they exceed M$5 million, whether by Malaysian or foreign interests. Except
37:1184:81025:12:12:115:541:328:12:Times:12:Times:F:for a few specific cases, IFC uses 100% for most stocks and 30% for banks and financial
37:1185:81112:12:20:115:173:316:12:Times:12:Times:F:institutions.
37:1186:81125:20:12:115:542:296:12:Times:12:Times:F:Mexico. Foreign portfolio investment is permitted in designated classes of shares, and
37:1187:81211:12:14:115:540:284:12:Times:12:Times:F:since May 1989 in most other shares through the use of the Nafinsa Trust arrangement.
37:1188:81296:14:12:115:543:270:12:Times:12:Times:F:It is now considered generally 100% investable, except for banks, where foreign ownership
37:1189:81385:12:18:115:213:258:12:Times:12:Times:F:is restricted to 30%.
37:1190:81406:18:19:115:301:240:12:Times:12:Times:F:Nigeria. Closed to foreign investment.
37:1191:81444:19:17:115:489:221:12:Times:12:Times:F:Pakistan. The market is considered 100% investable from February 22, 1991.
37:1192:81518:17:13:115:541:204:13:Times:13:Times:A:Philippines. National law requires that a minimum of 60% of the issued shares of do-
37:1193:81602:13:13:115:539:191:13:Times:13:Times:A:mestic corporations should be owned by Philippine nationals. To ensure compliance,
37:1194:81684:13:13:115:540:178:12:Times:12:Times:F:Philippine companies typically issued two classes of stock: "A" shares, which may be
37:1195:81768:13:13:115:540:165:12:Times:12:Times:F:traded only among Philippine nationals, and "B" shares, which may be traded to either
37:1196:81853:13:13:115:539:152:12:Times:12:Times:F:Philippine nationals or foreign investors and which usually amount to 40% of the total.
37:1197:81940:13:18:115:530:139:12:Times:12:Times:F:Mass media, retail trade and rural banking companies are closed to foreign investors.
37:1198:82025:18:14:114:540:121:13:Times:13:Times:A:Portugal. The market is considered generally 100% investable; some corporate statue
37:1199:82108:14:42:114:456:107:12:Times:12:Times:F:limitations apply, particularly regarding shares issued in privatization.
37:1200:82181:42:0:321:332:65:11:Times:11:Times:F:35
38:1201:82183:0:12:120:548:707:13:Times:13:Times:A:Taiwan. The market was opened to foreigners on January 1, 1991, though foreign in-
38:1202:82265:12:13:120:546:695:12:Times:12:Times:F:vestors must meet high registration requirements and total cash inflows much meet high
38:1203:82351:13:13:121:547:682:12:Times:12:Times:F:registration requirements and total cash inflows from abroad cannot currently exceed an
38:1204:82438:13:13:120:548:669:12:Times:12:Times:F:official ceiling of $2.5 billion. There is a 10% limit on aggregate foreign ownership of
38:1205:82526:13:18:121:523:656:12:Times:12:Times:F:issued capital. The domestic transportation industry is closed to foreign investors.
38:1206:82610:18:13:120:546:638:12:Times:12:Times:F:Thailand. Various Thai law restrict foreign shareholdings in Thai companies engaged in
38:1207:82696:13:14:120:548:625:12:Times:12:Times:F:certain areas of business. The Banking Law restricts foreign ownership in banks to 49%.
38:1208:82783:14:12:120:547:611:12:Times:12:Times:F:The Alien Business Law, administered by the Ministry of Commerce, restricts foreign
38:1209:82866:12:14:120:545:599:12:Times:12:Times:F:ownership of stocks in specified sectors to 49%. In addition, other laws provide similar
38:1210:82954:14:13:120:547:585:12:Times:12:Times:F:restrictions on foreign ownership. Restrictions are also faced by foreign investors through
38:1211:83045:13:12:120:545:572:12:Times:12:Times:F:limits imposed by company by-laws which range from 15% to 65%. The Foreign Board
38:1212:83125:12:18:120:517:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:was established in 1988 to facilitate trading in shares registered in foreign names.
38:1213:83209:18:18:120:461:542:12:Times:12:Times:F:Turkey. The market is considered 100% investable from August 1989.
38:1214:83275:18:13:120:546:524:12:Times:12:Times:F:Venezuela. Non-financial stocks are considered generally 100% investable from January
38:1215:83360:13:18:121:534:511:12:Times:12:Times:F:1, 1990, but some restricted classes do exist. Bank stocks are currently not available.
38:1216:83447:18:415:121:546:493:12:Times:12:Times:F:Zimbabwe. Effectively closed to foreign investment by virtue of severe exchange controls.
38:1217:83536:415:0:326:338:78:12:Times:12:Times:F:36
